  • The four hyperscalers' combined data-center investment this year: ~$700B
💡 Big-picture link

Either could move the market. A capex cut signal → semis plunge. An inflation-and-hikes signal → growth stocks plunge. Conversely, capex maintained plus a dovish Powell → the rally continues.

📋 Weekly Summaries

Only the week's major shifts, market meaning and next watchpoints

Week of July 20–24, 2026
In progress
Key shifts
  • Moonshot's Kimi K3 nearly closed the quality gap at much lower prices, validating a more capital-efficient Chinese AI model.
  • Alphabet's cloud growth impressed, but shares fell after capex rose toward $205B; Tesla's quarterly profit missed Wall Street by 37%.
  • Brent climbed 36% from July 2 toward $94, while BOJ tightening risk and higher long yields raised the discount-rate burden.
  • Smart-money selling and TSMC pricing power suggested AI margin may migrate from models toward silicon and infrastructure.
Bottom line: China is narrowing the technology gap with less capital, while US platforms must prove returns on ever-larger spending. Watch: oil, Chinese-model traffic, Alphabet capex returns and the BOJ.
Week of July 13–17, 2026
Complete
  • Hormuz reclosed, US strikes resumed and Bab el-Mandeb risk widened the conflict to multiple chokepoints.
  • CPI and PPI fell, but energy effects and renewed oil risk limited the disinflation signal.
  • TSMC fell despite 77% profit growth, exposing the cost of crowded positioning.
Bottom line: Positioning and energy risk overpowered good inflation and earnings news.
Week of July 6–10, 2026
Complete
  • Trump declared the truce over as Korean equities entered a bear market.
  • AI remained intact as a theme, but markets repriced it against higher funding costs and real profitability.
Bottom line: The AI trade shifted from growth expectations to financing cost and monetization.
Week of June 29–July 3, 2026
Complete
  • Weak breadth in the Magnificent Seven and yen pressure foreshadowed the July reversal.
  • Cloud leasing and new model launches highlighted both AI infrastructure excess and intensifying competition.
Week of June 22–26, 2026
Complete
  • Hot PCE supported the hawkish rate path while Chinese AI strength contrasted with OpenAI profitability concerns.
  • Defense stocks and prediction-market bets benefited from failed negotiations.
Week of June 15–19, 2026

  • The Iran peace framework failed at the last minute as the Fed and BOJ turned more hawkish.
  • Restrictions on non-US access to Anthropic models showed that AI competition had acquired national borders.
Bottom line: The peace and rate pillars of the Q2 rally weakened together.
Week of June 8–12, 2026
Complete
  • SpaceX completed the largest IPO on record at a $1.78T valuation, while OpenAI also entered the listing process.
  • Inflation and central-bank decisions tested how long high rates could coexist with premium valuations.
Earlier Q2 weeks
Apr–Jun
  • Record earnings, Warsh's confirmation, oil above $120 and rising AI capex drove the rally toward its peak.
  • OpenAI's target miss, the UAE's OPEC exit and muted stock reactions to record results introduced the first durable cracks.
Quarter takeaway: Q2 ended with stronger earnings but weaker assumptions around peace, rates and AI monetization.

February 2026
The Supreme Court struck down the tariffs, and before the month was out the war began — the hinge of everything
Feb 20 SCOTUS
IEEPA struck down
The legal basis for emergency tariffs collapses; the system is rebuilt
Feb 27
War with Iran
Hormuz choked — energy, inflation and rates hit at once
Inflation expectations
+100 bps
1–2yr swaps right after the war; year-end Fed expectations +75bps
The Fed
Warsh named
With the DOJ's Powell inquiry closed, confirmation came into view (May 15)
🌐 Politics
  • Feb 20: the Supreme Court ruled IEEPA tariffs unconstitutional — ending the year-old grammar of "emergency → presidential discretion." Tariffs had to be rebuilt on Section 232, 301 and other specific statutes
  • Feb 27: war between the US and Iran — the Strait of Hormuz tightened and the energy supply chain took a direct hit; the constant behind every macro question since
  • The Fed handover firmed up around Warsh, known for favoring QT — pressure on long yields, not relief
📈 Markets
  • Right after the war began, 1–2yr inflation expectations rose 100bps and year-end Fed-rate expectations +75bps — scrapping the easing story wholesale
  • The war split the market in two: after Feb 27, every major MSCI market except tech, Korea and Taiwan turned negative — a fact the index would hide for four months
  • The IEEPA ruling was a short-term positive (uncertainty removed) but left the refund question and a fiscal hole
💻 Tech
  • With everything else shaking, AI demand was the only certain growth — this is where the chip concentration hardened
  • Memory shortages fed price inflation and sent forward estimates for Samsung, SK Hynix and Micron sharply higher (a preview of May's $1T club)
🤖 AI
  • Software's weakness predates the Iran conflict — AI disrupting incumbents plus higher-for-longer rates straining their debt
  • SpaceX, OpenAI and Anthropic listing talks turned into a valuation race

🌐 Politics
  • May 12, Geneva: the US cut China tariffs 145%→30% and China cut 125%→10% for 90 days. Trump warned the cuts could be reversed if talks stall
  • May 8: a first deal with the UK — some Section 232 relief, but the 10% IEEPA baseline remained
  • On the Gulf tour, Saudi Arabia pledged $600B into US AI firms — inbound investment replaced tariffs as the headline instrument
📈 Markets
  • May 12: S&P +3.2%, Nasdaq +4.3% → positive for the year by May 13, erasing April's crash
  • May 16: Moody's downgraded the US (Aaa→Aa1), projecting deficits near 9% of GDP by 2035 and $4T more over a decade if tax cuts are extended
  • Late-month threats of 50% on the EU and 25% on Apple rattled markets again — fatigue at the reused bargaining chip
💻 Tech
  • A Gulf AI deal rush: Nvidia, AMD and Amazon signed datacenter agreements — oil money filled the gap where capital exists but power doesn't
  • The 25% Apple tariff threat turned "build iPhones in America" pressure into single-company risk
🤖 AI
  • Claude 4 (Opus and Sonnet) launched — the coding-agent race began in earnest
  • Sovereign-fund AI projects like Saudi Arabia's Humain spread the concept of "AI sovereignty"
April 2025
Liberation Day and the bond market's revolt — what turned the president wasn't stocks, it was Treasuries
Apr 2
Reciprocal
10% universal + up to 50% on 57 countries — the biggest since 1930
Apr 2–4
−4,000 pts
The Dow's worst two-day fall ever; S&P −11% in a week
30-year yield
+54 bps
Biggest three-day jump since 1982 → the Apr 9 pause
Apr 9 rebound
+9.52%
S&P's best day since 2008; Nasdaq +12.16%
🌐 Politics
  • Apr 2, "Liberation Day": EO 14257 signed in the Rose Garden declared the trade deficit a national emergency and used IEEPA for 10% on everything (Apr 5) plus up to 50% on 57 countries (Apr 9) — the largest hike since Smoot-Hawley
  • Apr 9: a 90-day pause for everyone except China. Trump: people were getting "a little bit yippy… I was watching the bond market"
  • Apr 11: smartphones, computers and other electronics exempted. Bessent took the lead on trade; Navarro was sidelined
📈 Markets
  • Apr 2–4: the Dow fell 4,000 points — its worst two-day drop in history; the S&P lost 11% in five sessions
  • The real event was in bonds: the 10-year fell to 3.86% on Apr 4, then surged to 4.5% by Apr 9; the 30-year jumped 54bps in three days, the most since 1982. Stocks, bonds and the dollar fell together — "we are being treated like a problematic emerging market" (Summers)
  • Minutes after the pause: S&P +9.52% (best since 2008), Nasdaq +12.16% — one of the great single days on record
  • Gold kept climbing and the dollar index fell — the first substantive doubt about American exceptionalism
💻 Tech
  • Apr 11: phones, laptops and chips exempted — Apple and peers snapped back, though a promised separate semiconductor tariff kept uncertainty alive
  • Supply-chain redesign accelerated as India and Vietnam were re-priced against each country's tariff rate
🤖 AI
  • Through the chaos, hyperscaler capex guidance held — reinforcing the belief that AI is immune to the cycle
  • China export controls forced Nvidia to book H20-related charges — politics landing directly in the P&L
March 2025
Tariffs actually took effect and stocks fell into correction — the month the bill arrived

🌐 Politics
  • Mar 4: 25% on Canada and Mexico and another 10% on China (20% total) took effect; Canada retaliated on $21B of US goods within hours
  • Mar 5–7: autos and then all USMCA-qualifying goods were exempted — cementing the announce → impose → retreat pattern
  • Mar 26: 25% tariffs on imported cars announced for April. The Signal group-chat leak damaged trust in the national-security team
📈 Markets
  • Mar 13: the S&P 500 entered a formal 10% correction — three weeks after a record high
  • The Magnificent 7 dragged the index down; gold kept setting records as the "tariffs = uncertainty" hedge
  • The Fed held while cutting growth forecasts and raising inflation forecasts — the first stagflation scare of the term
💻 Tech
  • Nvidia's GTC (Mar 18): Blackwell Ultra and the next roadmap unveiled — and the stock shrugged
  • Apple delayed its Siri overhaul to next year, hardening the "Apple is behind on AI" story
  • Talk of semiconductor tariffs pushed supply-chain relocation onto every earnings call
🤖 AI
  • After the DeepSeek shock, the low-cost model race spread — inference cost became the industry's central argument
  • Washington weighed tightening chip export controls on China further
  • "AI capex must shrink" vs "cheaper compute means more demand" (Jevons paradox) hardened into the two camps
February 2025
How to use tariffs as a weapon — announce, delay, re-announce — and the crack beneath a record high

Reciprocal memo

Feb 19 — the peak the rest of H1 fell from
🌐 Politics
  • Feb 1: tariffs imposed under the IEEPA emergency statute — a new grammar for tariffs by presidential discretion. Feb 3: Canada and Mexico paused for a month
  • Feb 10: steel and aluminum exemptions killed → Feb 13: the reciprocal-tariff memo (VAT counts as unfair)
  • DOGE's federal cuts spilled into litigation. Feb 28: the televised Oval Office clash with Zelenskyy made alliance risk a market variable
📈 Markets
  • Feb 19: the S&P 500 hit a record — and that day became the ceiling for the first half
  • Softening sentiment and retail sales plus tariff uncertainty drove risk-off into month-end
  • The market's "tariffs are just a bargaining chip" optimism faced its first real test
💻 Tech
  • DeepSeek aftershocks made the justification for Big Tech capex the earnings season's biggest question
  • Alexa+ (Feb 26) and peers: the race to graft LLMs onto existing products began in earnest
  • Tighter chip export rules started showing up in Asian supply-chain share prices
🤖 AI
  • A release rush: xAI's Grok 3, Anthropic's Claude 3.7 Sonnet (Feb 24), OpenAI's GPT-4.5 (Feb 27)
  • Reasoning models became the new axis of competition — the argument shifted from raw capability to performance per dollar
  • Under the new White House AI and crypto czar (David Sacks), deregulation was the clear default
January 2025
Trump 2.0 begins — an executive-order blitz, a $500B Stargate, and the DeepSeek shock

🌐 Politics
  • Jan 20: a record number of first-day executive orders — a border emergency, exits from the Paris accord and WHO, a federal hiring freeze, a regulatory freeze
  • Pardons for about 1,500 people charged over Jan 6 (14 sentences commuted) — an immediate political shock
  • DOGE formally created under Musk; the birthright-citizenship order drew lawsuits within hours. TikTok's ban was paused for 75 days
📈 Markets
  • Jan 27: the Nasdaq fell 3.1% as the AI trade repriced; the VIX jumped 45% in a day
  • AI-adjacent power plays collapsed: Constellation Energy −21%, Vistra −28%, Vertiv −30% — on fears of less electricity demand
  • An inauguration rally that reversed hard by month-end: the technology shock outweighed the policy story
💻 Tech
  • Jan 21: Stargate, a $500B venture (OpenAI, Oracle, SoftBank) — AI infrastructure declared a national-scale race
  • Jan 27: Nvidia lost $589B in one day — double the previous record ($279B) and the biggest in US history
  • Broadcom −17.4%, AMD −6.4%, ASML −7% — the selloff swept Asian and European chipmakers too
🤖 AI
  • The DeepSeek R1 shock: an open-source model claimed to be built in two months for under $6M, reportedly beating OpenAI's o1 on several tests
  • Andreessen called it AI's "Sputnik moment"; Bernstein countered that the models look fantastic but aren't miracles
  • Trump revoked Biden's AI-safety executive order — choosing speed over guardrails

📊 Quarterly Summary

Once a quarter closes, we keep only what happened and why — across four strands: politics, markets, tech and AI.

Q2 2026 Apr – Jun
In one line: the war never ended, but AI covered for it — so stocks hit records, and from late June the cover began to slip.
🌐 Politics — at home and abroad
  • The Iran war was the quarter's background noise. Ten weeks after Trump declared Iran's navy and air force "demolished," Iran kept choking the Strait of Hormuz. Oil topped $120 in May; on June 1 Iran vowed to block Hormuz "completely" (oil +5.9%)
  • A mid-June peace framework → canceled at the last minute on Friday June 19. It revived as a ceasefire on June 29 — which itself collapsed on July 8–9
  • The Fed was the biggest political event: Powell's final FOMC on May 1 (he stays on as a governor), then Warsh confirmed 54–45 on May 15 — the slimmest margin ever. On June 30 the Supreme Court ruled the president cannot fire Fed governors: Trump lost, but he had already installed his own chair
  • US–China settled into "managed competition": a May Trump–Xi summit in Beijing (three years of "strategic stability," 200 Boeings) alongside June's tariff sequel (12.5% on Korea) and the G7's push away from Chinese rare earths
Why it happened

Iran learned it could keep its regime and control the waterway, and the US had no cheap way to reverse that. So diplomacy could only paper over the gap with a deliberately ambiguous document — Authers called it not a Memorandum of Understanding but a Memorandum of Misunderstanding. July's rupture was inside that margin of error from the start.

📈 Markets
  • The S&P 500 booked its best quarter since 2020 (June 30) — even as University of Michigan consumer sentiment hit its worst reading since the survey began in 1978. Virtually the entire gain came from semiconductors
  • The Shiller CAPE reached its highest since Sept 2000, exceeding even the eve of the 1929 crash (June 1); sales multiples were the highest in history
  • Bonds and FX: May's 30-year yield hit a 19-year high ("the great bond car wreck, in slow motion"). Warsh's June 18 hawkish surprise sent TIPS real yields to a one-year high and gave the dollar its strongest rise of the year. The average year-end dot moved from 3.24% to 3.83%
  • Inflation: headline CPI topped 4% for the first time in three years (June 10). The ECB hiked; the BOJ raised rates to their highest since 1995 — while the UK's expected hikes fell from three to one as oil cooled
  • The debasement trade broke: for the half, Brent +19.8% vs bitcoin −33.3%. Warsh's hawkishness dismantled the logic of gold and crypto
  • Cracks at quarter-end: SK Hynix −13.2% on June 24 (its 2x leveraged ETF −26.4%); investors began rotating out of the Magnificent Seven on June 30
Why it happened

With the war pushing inflation up, hopes of cuts were dead — yet stocks rose anyway, for one reason: AI profits genuinely exploded. But that changed what the index was: strip out tech, Korea and Taiwan, and major MSCI markets were all down since the war began (Authers, June 11). Q2's rally wasn't "the economy is good"; it was one sector covering for everything else — which is why, when that sector wobbled, everything wobbled.

💻 Tech
  • The $1 trillion club filled up with chipmakers: after Samsung in May, Micron (+19.3%) and SK Hynix crossed the line hours apart on May 27. The biggest chipmakers now rival or surpass Meta
  • Leadership changed hands: of the S&P's 672-point rally, the Mag 7 contributed 160 points and seven SOX chipmakers 289 — strip out Nvidia and it's 79 vs 369. "Short software, buy the SOX" returned 150% in the half
  • The SaaSpocalypse: the S&P 1500 Software Index shed a third of its value in eight months. Direct lending to SaaS firms grew from $8B in 2015 to $538B in 2025
  • The biggest IPO rush ever: SpaceX debuted at $1.78T on June 12 and hit $2.75T three days later, overtaking Amazon; OpenAI (6/9) and Anthropic (6/1) filed
  • "iFlation" (June 26): Apple raised prices because AI-driven memory costs exploded — AI's bill reached the consumer price tag
Why it happened

One realization reorganized the market: hyperscalers won't hog AI's profits — they must spend enormously, and that money goes to suppliers (chips). Capital rotated from software and platforms into infrastructure. The catch: this was a zero-sum rotation, not a rising tide. Virtually all the free cash hyperscalers generate now goes to capex (Microsoft sat 28% below its high), and tech capex passed 7% of real GDP — the level at which housing bubbles burst in the US, Japan and Spain.

🤖 AI
  • The model contest changed shape: April 30 earnings confirmed the pivot from "we offer the best model" to "we host every model — a marketplace" (Apple did the same, bolting outside models onto Siri at WWDC)
  • Anthropic passed OpenAI (May 29: $965B vs $852B); unveiled "Fable" on June 10 and Claude Fable 5 on July 1
  • AI became a national-security category: in mid-June Washington ordered Anthropic to switch off its most powerful models for all non-US citizens ("could chill the whole AI trade"); Mythos and Fable prompted export restrictions
  • China closed the gap: Huawei's "Logic Folding" breakthrough (May 27), Zhipu's surge (late June), and reports that Chinese AI was catching stalled-out US models (June 29)
  • The temperature started dropping: Oracle fell 25% from its peak on June 10 after disclosing soaring capex — the market began asking "where does the money come from?"
Why it happened

In Q2, AI moved from a technology race to a capital-and-politics race. As the performance gap narrowed (marketplaces, Chinese catch-up), the contest shifted to ① who secures chips and power ② who gets government permission. That's why even great earnings couldn't lift prices: financing strain and regulatory risk did the work — the real engine of the late-June and July repricing.

Q1 2026 Jan – Mar
In one line: the tariff regime collapsed in court and a Fed handover loomed — then March's Iran war dropped an energy shock on top.
🌐 Politics — at home and abroad
  • The IEEPA ruling struck down the emergency-powers basis for Trump 2.0's tariffs — moving trade policy from presidential discretion back to law and Congress
  • The Fed handover came into view as Powell's term wound down. Trump wanted a 3% inflation target (which would make cuts easy); markets expected an obedient dove
  • Feb 27: war between the US and Iran, choking the Strait of Hormuz and hitting the energy supply chain — the constant behind every macro question thereafter
Why it happened

Q1's character was policy discretion colliding with institutions: tariffs stopped by courts, Fed capture limited to appointments (and later blocked outright by the Supreme Court). But geopolitics filled the vacuum — a shock no court could enjoin arrived in March.

📈 Markets
  • The war split the year in two: after Feb 27, every major MSCI market except tech, Korea and Taiwan turned negative — a fact the index would hide for the next two quarters
  • Inflation expectations jumped: 1–2yr breakevens rose 100bps right after the war began, and year-end Fed-rate expectations rose 75bps — scrapping the "easing cycle" scenario wholesale
  • Hard money peaked: precious metals hit records early in the year, and bitcoin's all-time high dated to October. Both were primed to turn
  • Energy was the only winner — briefly. Energy stocks surged in March, but across Trump 2.0 they ended up matching the rest of the market, because the oil shock diffused into everything
Why it happened

A war is a supply shock, and central banks have no good answer: hike and growth dies, cut and prices run. So Q1 markets abandoned the easing story — and the vacuum was filled by the one remaining bull case, AI earnings growth. The seed of Q2's crowding was planted here.

💻 Tech
  • The chip concentration began: with everything else shaking, AI demand was the only certain growth story. Memory shortages fed price inflation, and forward earnings estimates for Samsung, SK Hynix and Micron began climbing fast
  • Software's decline had already started — the S&P 1500 Software Index's weakness predates the Iran conflict (AI disrupting incumbents' models, plus higher-for-longer rates straining the debt behind them)
  • The IPO pipeline formed: SpaceX, OpenAI and Anthropic listing talks turned into a valuation race through the quarter
Why it happened

Scarcity did it: "certain growth in an uncertain world" pulled capital into one place. What later became clear is that this was a positioning problem, not a valuation one — in Q2 the earnings estimates caught up, completing a bubble that looked cheap.

🤖 AI
  • AI supremacy became national strategy — both Washington and Beijing began treating AI as a security asset; rare earths and compute joined the list of "new strategic assets"
  • The frontier race intensified, spilling from models into talent and capital (leading to April's Karpathy hire and the rest)
  • The regulatory shadow appeared: the EU began restricting access to top-tier models — the precursor to June's US order freezing Anthropic for non-citizens
Why it happened

Once models became good enough to find security vulnerabilities, AI stopped being a product and started being treated as a weapons category. That shift in perception settled in during Q1 — and in Q2 it became the reality that a single government letter can halt even the best company overnight.

Q4 2025 Oct – Dec
In one line: the longest shutdown ever left the Fed deciding without data, the AI-bubble debate moved prices for the first time — and crypto broke first.
🌐 Politics — at home and abroad
  • Oct 1 – Nov 12: a 43-day shutdown, the longest in US history, over ACA subsidies, with 14 failed Senate votes. CBO: ~$11B permanently lost; ~$15B a week. The core dispute survived intact
  • Oct 10: a 100% tariff threat against China answering rare-earth controls, later softened. Oct 24: Scope cut the US to AA-
  • Nov 5: the Supreme Court heard the IEEPA case — putting tariffs-by-emergency-power itself on trial (ruling to come in 2026)
  • The year's closing question was who chairs the Fed next, with Powell's term ending in May
Why it happened

Once Q3's instruments became hard to reverse, the pushback came back in institutional form — Congress via appropriations, the courts via the tariff statute, the agencies via governance-based downgrades. The tell: 43 days of fighting settled nothing, which meant the same standoff would return in 2026.

📈 Markets
  • Two more cuts (Oct 29, Dec 10) took rates to 3.50–3.75% — three for the year — though November's minutes briefly collapsed December odds from 98% to 32%
  • Powell described policy as operating in a "fog" without statistics — an unprecedented data blackout
  • A $1T crypto deleveraging: from October's $126K peak to a $80,255 flash low on Nov 21; $3.79B of ETF outflows; 93% of liquidations were longs; still only ~$87K at year-end
  • Gold set records above $4,000; stocks rallied into year-end — the asset classes split for the first time
Why it happened

Q4's lesson was that cuts don't lift everything. Bitcoin traded as leveraged Nasdaq, so it broke first when the rate path wobbled (outflows → liquidation cascade); gold rose on fiscal distrust; only equities held, on AI earnings. Liquidity had begun flowing selectively — a preview of 2026's "Warsh sank the debasement trade."

💻 Tech
  • Big Tech raised capex across the board: Alphabet $91–93B, Meta $70–72B, Microsoft $34.9B in a quarter — and the stocks still hit records
  • It became consensus that AI spending is a core driver of US GDP — the economy taken hostage by AI
  • Nvidia's Nov 19 beat couldn't hold a bid for a day — the first sign that even great results can't lift the stock
Why it happened

The regime where higher capex meant a higher stock ended this quarter, because the market changed the arithmetic: capex is future depreciation, and the money is borrowed. The argument narrowed to circular deals, depreciation and power — the three items that keep coming due through the first half of 2026 (the Oracle shock, the token-spend slump).

🤖 AI
  • Oct 28: OpenAI completed its restructuring (a PBC, Microsoft at ~27%) — opening the path to an IPO
  • Oct 6: the AMD–OpenAI 6GW deal with warrants spread the supplier-customer equity entanglement
  • Prominent shorts went public against AI infrastructure, launching the depreciation-accounting fight
Why it happened

This is the quarter AI became a financial structure. Nonprofit-to-PBC conversion, chip contracts wired with warrants, SPV and bond financing — all of it engineering to build supply before demand is proven. The technology argument receded; accounting and funding became the real variables in AI share prices.

Q3 2025 Jul – Sep
In one line: the quarter policy made prices directly — tax cuts, legal stablecoins and the first rate cut landed together, the state took equity in a chipmaker, and AI started funding itself.
🌐 Politics — at home and abroad
  • Jul 4: the One Big Beautiful Bill (Senate 51–50): 2017 cuts made permanent, the debt ceiling raised $5T, Medicaid cut 12% — adding $2.8–3T to deficits over a decade
  • Jul 18: the GENIUS Act, America's first major crypto law (1:1 stablecoin reserves). July brought 15% deals with Japan and the EU → tariffs resumed Aug 7
  • State capitalism arrived: the government took a ~10% stake in Intel ($8.9B), and Nvidia and AMD bought export licenses by handing over 15% of China revenue
  • Pressure on the Fed became routine: the BLS chief fired (Aug 1), Lisa Cook threatened with removal (Aug 22, in court by September), Miran confirmed to the Board
Why it happened

Once Q2 revealed that tariffs get reversed, the administration switched to instruments that stick — tax law, legislation, equity (Intel) and appointments. Tariffs were a bargaining chip; these are not easily undone. It's the quarter US industrial policy moved from "rules and subsidies" to the state as shareholder.

📈 Markets
  • Sep 17: the term's first 25bp cut, with dots pointing to two more. Powell: "there is no risk-free path" (hot inflation vs a soft labor market)
  • Aug 22: Powell's Jackson Hole opening sent the Dow up 800 points to a record and cut odds from 70% to 91.5%
  • Crypto's market cap topped $4T right after the GENIUS vote; Nvidia crossed $4T on Jul 9
  • Tariffs came back on Aug 7 to a shrug — immunity to policy headlines was complete
Why it happened

Q3's rally was the first time liquidity and earnings worked together. Trade deals converged on 15% and cleared the uncertainty; a cooling labor market turned the Fed; AI earnings kept coming. The catch: the cut came because jobs were weak, not because growth was strong — and that contradiction (soft economy, strong assets) runs straight through the first half of 2026.

💻 Tech
  • Jul 9: Nvidia at $4T, a first; on Sep 18 its $5B stake lifted Intel 23%, completing the revival story
  • Sep 10: Oracle disclosed ~$300B of AI backlog and the stock exploded — while Moody's flagged customer-concentration and funding risk
  • Power became the confirmed bottleneck, and nuclear emerged as AI's answer (BofA: a $10T opportunity)
Why it happened

AI investment became visible as a number — the backlog (RPO) — and prices exploded. But a backlog is a promise, not cash, which is exactly what Moody's flagged: who pays, and with whose money? The question was deferred while the stock went first — and the bill arrives with the −25% Oracle shock in June 2026.

🤖 AI
  • Sep 22: Nvidia pledged up to $100B to OpenAI — the seller financing the buyer, a circular deal
  • August's MIT report ("95% of AI pilots show no return") triggered the first ROI skepticism; GPT-5 landed quietly
  • July's AI Action Plan rested on deregulation, export promotion and power — while export control mutated into a 15% revenue tax
Why it happened

AI's structure forces you to build supply (chips, datacenters) before demand is proven. So suppliers start lending to customers — the same vendor financing that defined the telecom bubble. That a "95% show no return" report and a "$100B investment" landed in the same quarter is the whole story of this phase.

Q2 2025 Apr – Jun
In one line: it began with the largest tariffs in a century and ended at record highs — what turned the president was bonds, not stocks, and once markets learned that, they discounted every threat that followed.
🌐 Politics — at home and abroad
  • Apr 2, Liberation Day — 10% on everything plus up to 50% on 57 countries under IEEPA; the biggest hike since Smoot-Hawley in 1930. Apr 9: a 90-day pause for all but China (Trump: "I was watching the bond market")
  • May 12, Geneva: China tariffs cut 145%→30% (China 125%→10%) for 90 days. May 8: a first deal with the UK
  • May 16: Moody's downgrade (Aaa→Aa1) — all three agencies have now stripped the top rating, with extended tax cuts seen adding $4T to deficits over a decade
  • Jun 13–24: the 12-day Israel–Iran war, ending in a ceasefire after US strikes on Fordow. At home: the National Guard in LA and nationwide "No Kings" protests
Why it happened

April proved that this administration's binding constraint is the Treasury market. At −11% in stocks the line was "my policies will never change"; when the 30-year jumped 54bps in three days, the pause came within hours. Markets applied the lesson immediately, discounting every later threat (50% on the EU, 25% on Apple) as "it'll be walked back" — which is why tariff headlines rapidly lost their power to move prices.

📈 Markets
  • Apr 2–4: the Dow −4,000 points (its worst two days ever) → Apr 9: S&P +9.52% (best since 2008) and Nasdaq +12.16%. Volatility spiked ten standard deviations above its long-term average
  • Stocks, bonds and the dollar fell together — an emerging-market pattern, in Summers' phrase. The 10-year went from 3.86% (Apr 4) to 4.5% (Apr 9)
  • Positive for the year by May 13 → records on Jun 27 — a full round trip in three months
  • Even with a war in June, oil finished the truce below its pre-war level — cementing the view that geopolitics is short
Why it happened

The V-shape had two causes: ① the worst case (permanent full tariffs) left the table, and ② AI earnings actually showed up. From this, the market acquired a decisive habit — "bad news gets reversed" — the habit that let stocks hit records during a war in early 2026, and that removed every cushion when July finally broke.

💻 Tech
  • Apr 11: phones, laptops and chips were exempted — Big Tech became the trade war's de facto protected class
  • The Gulf tour produced an AI infrastructure rush including Saudi Arabia's $600B — oil money filling America's bottleneck, where capital exists but power doesn't
  • Jun 5: Circle's IPO soared, starting the crypto-infrastructure listing boom; Nvidia was back at records by late June
Why it happened

The trade war's biggest winner was, paradoxically, tech. Electronics exemptions let it dodge the cost, and while uncertainty froze everyone else's investment, the scarcity value of "certain growth" only rose. The concentration that began in Q1 hardened into structure in Q2.

🤖 AI
  • Jun 12: Meta put $14.3B into Scale AI (49%) and hired its founder; its new superintelligence lab pushed the talent war to sports-transfer economics
  • Claude 4 (May) made coding agents the first real killer app
  • The OpenAI–Microsoft contract dispute surfaced; export controls forced Nvidia's H20 write-downs
Why it happened

Once DeepSeek showed in Q1 that models can be replicated, competition moved from models to people, power and chips — the only things that can't be copied. Meta's $14.3B deal and the Gulf datacenter rush are two faces of the same logic — and the starting point of 2026's "capex at 7% of GDP" problem.

Q1 2025 Jan – Mar · Trump 2.0 begins
In one line: a new grammar opened — tariffs by presidential discretion — and DeepSeek broke the premise that AI is a game you win only with money.
🌐 Politics — at home and abroad
  • Jan 20: a record first-day blitz of executive orders — 78 Biden actions revoked, a border emergency, exits from the Paris accord and WHO, pardons for ~1,500 people charged over Jan 6, DOGE created, TikTok paused 75 days
  • Feb 1: IEEPA tariffs — 25% on Canada and Mexico, 10% on China, justified by a fentanyl and migration emergency → paused Feb 3 → in force Mar 4 → broad USMCA exemptions by Mar 7
  • Feb 13: the reciprocal-tariff memo (VAT as an unfair practice); Mar 12: steel and aluminum exemptions terminated; Mar 26: 25% auto tariffs announced
  • Feb 28: the Oval Office clash with Zelenskyy; March: the Signal chat leak — alliance and security-management risk entered the market's variables
Why it happened

The change was in the instrument. Tariffs set by emergency declaration and presidential discretion rather than legislation meant the real cost wasn't the rate — it was the knowledge that it could change tomorrow. As announce–pause–re-announce repeated, firms deferred investment. That pattern recurs all year (and eventually produces the 2026 IEEPA ruling).

📈 Markets
  • Feb 19: a record S&P 500 → Mar 13: a 10% correction — ceiling to correction in three weeks
  • Jan 27: the Nasdaq −3.1% on the DeepSeek repricing; the VIX +45% in a day; power plays collapsed (Constellation −21%, Vistra −28%)
  • Gold kept setting records — the hedge against tariff and policy uncertainty
  • The Fed held while cutting growth and raising inflation forecasts → the term's first stagflation debate
Why it happened

Q1's decline wasn't about earnings — it was the discount rate and uncertainty. Tariffs are a cost to firms, a price to consumers and a dilemma for the Fed, which weakened the assumption that rate cuts would rescue anyone. Then DeepSeek shook the equation that AI growth = chip revenue, always. Both pillars under the index wobbled at once.

💻 Tech
  • Jan 21: Stargate, $500B (OpenAI, Oracle, SoftBank) — AI infrastructure became a national-strategy project
  • Jan 27: Nvidia −17%, $589B erased in a day — the largest single-day wipeout in US market history, double the old record. Broadcom −17.4%, AMD −6.4%, ASML −7%
  • Mar 18: Nvidia's GTC unveiled Blackwell Ultra and the stock didn't move — the first sign that good news had stopped working
  • Apple pushed its Siri overhaul to next year — the AI gap between Big Tech names began to widen
Why it happened

DeepSeek asked one question: does AI really need this much money? If not, the entire premise behind astronomical spending on chips, datacenters and power collapses. Markets sold first and asked later. The debate was eventually settled by the Jevons argument — cheaper compute means more demand — which powered the late-2025 rally. But the fight over whether capex is justified starts here, and runs all the way to the Oracle shock in June 2026.

🤖 AI
  • DeepSeek R1 (January): claimed two months and under $6M to build, released open-source, and passed ChatGPT in the App Store. Andreessen called it AI's "Sputnik moment"
  • February's release rush: Grok 3, Claude 3.7 Sonnet (2/24), GPT-4.5 (2/27) — reasoning models became the new axis
  • Trump revoked Biden's AI-safety order — speed over guardrails — while pushing to tighten China export controls further
Why it happened

DeepSeek was built around export controls (trained on older H800 chips). So Washington's conclusion wasn't "controls failed" but "tighten them, and run faster ourselves" — the decisive step that moved AI from industrial policy into security policy. The order freezing Anthropic for non-US citizens in June 2026 has its roots right here.
